# Higham Chapter 20 Source Coverage Ledger

## Source and Scope

- Edition: Higham, *Accuracy and Stability of Numerical Algorithms*, 2nd ed. (SIAM, 2002), verified from repository metadata and the SIAM chapter PDF title metadata.
- Chapter: 20, "The Least Squares Problem".
- Source file: `References/1.9780898718027.ch20.pdf`.
- Printed pages: 381-406.
- Mode: core.
- Parallel split: 4.
- Planning documents consulted: `chapter_splitting/HIGHAM_PARALLEL_FORMALIZATION_BLUEPRINT.md`, Split 4 section of `chapter_splitting/split_primary_contracts.md`, and `chapter_splitting/chapter_index.md`.
- Baseline: `lake env lean` passed for `LSPerturbation.lean`, `LSQRSolve.lean`, and `LSNormalEquations.lean`; pre-existing worktree dirt was `.DS_Store`.
- Selected-scope gate: FAIL. The remaining selected Chapter 20 body work includes the Theorem 20.3 stored-Householder endgame, the sharper Theorem 20.4/Section 20.5 RHS coefficient, the full (20.18)-(20.19) spectral multiplicity and condition-number bridge, the positive-branch Walden--Karlson--Sun spectral lower-bound/attainment proof behind (20.21), and Theorem 20.9's GQR existence/reconstruction work. End-of-chapter exercises are reserved for benchmarks and are not counted as selected-scope targets.
- Bottleneck ledger: the active red-bottleneck entries for the repeated Chapter 20 blockers are recorded below.  One GPT Pro oracle consultation was attempted for the Theorem 20.9 pivot; it was generic/stalled, nothing from it was adopted, and the adopted route was verified locally in Lean.

## Active Bottleneck Ledger

These entries are active because repeated proof and audit passes have produced useful conditional infrastructure while leaving the same selected-scope foundation exposed.  Progress on these rows should be counted only when one of the listed next dependency theorems is proved, a listed route is ruled out with Lean/source evidence, or the theorem surface is corrected to match the source.  Do not add adjacent wrappers for these rows unless the wrapper closes one of the named dependencies.

Proof-source update: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaRHS_le_costF_of_feasible_finite_theta` and `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaRHS_le_etaF_of_finite_theta` now combine the `p = 0` exact-residual branch with the nonzero-expanded-residual branch and transfer the all-feasible pointwise lower bound to the infimum model `eta_F`.  The finite lower-bound side is closed under `0 <= theta`, `y != 0`, and nonzero source residual hypotheses; the source-block `sigma_min` constructive upper-bound branch is still open.  No GPT Pro oracle consultation was used for this update.

Proof-source update: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaRHS_le_etaF_of_positive_theta_not_isLeastSquaresMinimizer` derives the nonzero source-residual condition from the finite positive non-minimizer branch, and `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorEtaF_eq_formulaRHS_and_pos_of_positive_upper_certificate` uses that local lower-bound theorem to package the positive branch from only the remaining upper inequality `eta_F(y) <= RHS`.  The source-block `sigma_min` constructive upper-bound branch, eigenvalue branch formula, and `theta = infinity` limiting case remain open.  No GPT Pro oracle consultation was used for this update.

Proof-source update: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorEtaF_eq_formulaRHS_and_pos_of_phi_le_sigmaMin` specializes the positive upper-certificate handoff to the printed scalar branch `phi <= sigma_min [A phi(I-r r^+)]`.  The exact-fit perturbation gives the upper inequality, the finite-positive lower-bound side gives equality and positivity, and the source-block `sigma_min` construction, eigenvalue branch formula, and `theta = infinity` limiting case remain open.  No GPT Pro oracle consultation was used for this update.

Proof-source update: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorRankOneDeltaA`, `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorRankOneDeltaA_transpose_mul`, `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorRankOneDeltaA_frobNormSq`, `LSNormwiseBackwardErrorFeasible.rankOne_source_residual_witness`, `LSNormwiseBackwardErrorFeasible.exists_rankOne_source_residual_witness`, and `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorEtaF_le_rankOne_source_residual_witness` add the first concrete source-block upper-route construction for the WKS positive branch.  For any nonzero expanded residual `p`, the rank-one `DeltaA` realizes the left action `-A^T p`, has the exact Frobenius norm `||A^T p||_2^2 / ||p||_2^2` in the prescribed-action form, and with the matching `Delta b` makes `y` feasible for the perturbed least-squares problem; the existential package exposes those residual, action, and Frobenius facts, and the new `eta_F` theorem turns the construction into an explicit square-root upper bound.  This is still partial foundation: it does not extract a row-side `sigma_min` singular vector, prove the weighted cost is bounded by the printed RHS, close `eta_F(y) <= RHS` on the `sigma_min` branch, derive the eigenvalue branch formula, or handle `theta = infinity`.  No GPT Pro oracle consultation was used for this update.

Proof-source update: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorRankOneDeltaA_mulVec` and `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorEtaF_le_rankOne_source_residual_witness_expanded` expose the `DeltaA * y` term in the rank-one WKS witness and rewrite the square-root `eta_F` upper bound with the resulting explicit `Delta b` vector.  This closes the next algebraic dependency needed to compare the rank-one witness cost with a future source-block singular-vector certificate.  It is still partial foundation: it does not choose the row-side `sigma_min` vector, prove the witness cost is bounded by the printed RHS, close the source-block `sigma_min` branch, derive the eigenvalue branch formula, or handle `theta = infinity`.  No GPT Pro oracle consultation was used for this update.

Proof-source update: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorEtaF_le_formulaRHS_of_rankOne_expanded_cost_le_sigmaMin` packages the source-block `sigma_min` branch around the concrete rank-one witness: once a nonzero expanded residual `p` has the explicit expanded witness cost bounded by the source-block `sigma_min`, and the printed outer minimum selects that branch, the theorem proves `eta_F(y) <=` the right-hand side of (20.21).  This removes the generic upper-inequality handoff for the rank-one route, but it still leaves the genuine source-block singular-vector certificate, eigenvalue branch formula, and `theta = infinity` limiting case open.  No GPT Pro oracle consultation was used for this update.

Proof-source update: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorEtaF_eq_formulaRHS_and_pos_of_rankOne_expanded_cost_le_sigmaMin` combines the concrete rank-one `sigma_min` upper handoff with the already proved finite-positive WKS lower-bound theorem.  Under positive finite `theta`, nonzero `y`, non-minimizer and full-row-rank branch assumptions, the positive-branch equality and positivity now follow from the explicit expanded rank-one cost certificate rather than a generic `eta_F <= RHS` hypothesis.  The remaining open proof is still the actual source-block singular-vector certificate that supplies that expanded cost bound, plus the eigenvalue branch formula and `theta = infinity`.  No GPT Pro oracle consultation was used for this update.

Proof-source update: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorEtaF_le_rankOne_source_residual_witness_scaled` exposes the nonzero scalar freedom in the expanded rank-one WKS witness.  For a nonzero expanded residual candidate `p` and nonzero scalar `c`, it proves the same Frobenius/source-action term as the unscaled witness while replacing the explicit `Delta b` vector by `c * p - r - projection(p)`.  This is the next algebraic dependency for optimizing the rank-one witness against a source-block singular-vector certificate; it still does not choose the row-side `sigma_min` vector, prove the expanded witness cost bound, derive the eigenvalue branch formula, or handle `theta = infinity`.  No GPT Pro oracle consultation was used for this update.

Proof-source update: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorEtaF_le_formulaRHS_of_rankOne_scaled_cost_le_sigmaMin` and `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorEtaF_eq_formulaRHS_and_pos_of_rankOne_scaled_cost_le_sigmaMin` package the scaled rank-one WKS route at the same source-facing surfaces as the unscaled certificate.  Once a nonzero scalar `c` and nonzero expanded residual `p` satisfy the explicit scaled witness cost bound against the source-block `sigma_min`, the first theorem proves `eta_F(y) <= RHS`; under positive finite `theta`, nonzero `y`, non-minimizer, and full source-block row-rank assumptions, the second combines that scaled upper handoff with the already proved lower-bound side to obtain equality and positivity.  The actual singular-vector construction supplying the scaled cost bound, the eigenvalue branch formula, and `theta = infinity` remain open.  No GPT Pro oracle consultation was used for this update.

Proof-source update: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorRankOne_scaled_cost_sqrt_le_of_sq_le` and `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorEtaF_le_formulaRHS_of_rankOne_scaled_sq_cost_le_sigmaMin` convert the scaled rank-one WKS upper handoff to the division-free squared form expected from the remaining singular-vector algebra.  The generic bridge proves that a certificate `||u||_2^2 + theta^2 ||q||_2^2 ||p||_2^2 <= sigma^2 ||p||_2^2` implies the square-root witness cost bound, and the source-facing theorem applies it with `sigma = sigma_min [A phi(I-r r^+)]` to prove `eta_F(y) <= RHS` when the outer minimum selects that branch.  The singular-vector construction that supplies the squared certificate, the eigenvalue branch formula, and `theta = infinity` remain open.  No GPT Pro oracle consultation was used for this update.

Proof-source update: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaMatrix_transpose_vecNorm2Sq_eq` proves the unconditional squared transpose-action expansion for the WKS source block `[A phi(I-r r^+)]`: for arbitrary `p`, the squared norm of the transposed action splits as `||A^T p||_2^2 + phi^2 ||(I-r r^+)p||_2^2`.  This is the algebraic source-block comparison form needed before a genuine row-side `sigma_min` singular-vector certificate can feed the squared rank-one WKS cost bridge.  It still does not choose the minimizing vector, prove the scaled witness cost bound, derive the eigenvalue branch formula, or handle `theta = infinity`.  No GPT Pro oracle consultation was used for this update.

Proof-source update: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorRankOne_scaled_sq_cost_le_of_source_transpose_sq_le` and `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorEtaF_le_formulaRHS_of_rankOne_scaled_source_transpose_cert` connect the source-block singular-vector route to the scaled rank-one WKS upper handoff.  The bridge proves that a source-transpose upper certificate together with a right-projector comparison implies the division-free squared rank-one cost certificate, and the source-facing theorem applies this bridge to prove `eta_F(y) <= RHS` on the `sigma_min` branch.  The actual minimizing-vector/source-transpose certificate, the projector comparison from the optimal scalar choice, the eigenvalue branch formula, and `theta = infinity` remain open.  No GPT Pro oracle consultation was used for this update.

Proof-source update: `complexMatrixSingularValue_mul_norm_gramEigenvectorBasis_eq_norm_euclideanLin`, `complexMatrixSingularValue_exists_attaining_vector`, and `complexMatrixSingularValue_exists_attaining_vector_sq` add a checked shared spectral attainment witness for the singular-value API underlying the row-side `sigma_min` wrapper.  This closes the generic complex Gram-eigenvector attainment dependency; the WKS row remains open because the witness still has to be transported to a real vector for the source block `[A phi(I-r r^+)]`, then combined with the scaled rank-one projector comparison.  No GPT Pro oracle consultation was used for this update.

Proof-source update: `realRectToCMatrix_last_singularValue_exists_real_attaining_vector_sq` transports the last-singular-value attainment foundation to real rectangular matrices.  For any real `A`, it produces a nonzero real vector whose squared action by `A` equals the square of the last singular value of the complexification times the vector squared norm.  This closes the real-attainment dependency needed before specializing to the row-side source block; the WKS row remains open until the theorem is instantiated for `[A phi(I-r r^+)]^T` and combined with the scaled rank-one projector comparison.  No GPT Pro oracle consultation was used for this update.

Proof-source update: `lsRealRectSigmaMinRow_exists_transpose_attaining_vector_sq` and `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaMatrixSigmaMin_exists_transpose_attaining_vector_sq` specialize the real-attainment witness to the row-side `sigma_min` API and the WKS source block `[A phi(I-r r^+)]`.  The source-block theorem now provides a nonzero real `p` with exact squared transpose-action equality, which supplies the `hsource` half of the existing scaled rank-one source-transpose certificate route.  The WKS upper branch remains open because the scaled rank-one projector comparison and optimal scalar choice still have to be proved locally.  No GPT Pro oracle consultation was used for this update.

Proof-source update: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorRankOne_scaled_q_projected_eq_neg`, `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorRankOne_scaled_q_projector_lower_bound`, and `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorRankOne_scaled_q_optimal_vecNorm2Sq` close the scalar-choice algebra for the scaled rank-one WKS witness.  They prove that the free scalar changes only the component parallel to `p`, that every scalar leaves an unavoidable orthogonal component at least `||(I-p p^+)r||_2^2`, and that the explicit optimal scalar realizes exactly that projected residual.  This is progress on the listed optimal-scalar dependency, but it also shows that the current rank-one source-transpose projector-comparison route cannot be closed merely by choosing the scalar; the remaining source-block `sigma_min` upper branch needs a stronger perturbation construction or a different WKS-specific comparison route, plus the eigenvalue branch formula and `theta = infinity`.  No GPT Pro oracle consultation was used for this update.

Proof-source update: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorRankOne_scaled_projector_comparison_not_of_projected_ne_zero` formalizes the route-elimination consequence of the scalar-choice lemmas.  For positive finite `theta`, nonzero `y`, nonzero `r` and `p`, and nonzero projected source-block component `(I-r r^+)p`, it proves that the right-projector comparison required by the current scaled rank-one source-transpose handoff is impossible for every scalar.  This rules out the nondegenerate scalar-only projector-comparison route; the next WKS upper-branch work must use a stronger perturbation construction, a degenerate projected-residual subcase, or a different source-specific comparison route.  No GPT Pro oracle consultation was used for this update.

Proof-source update: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorRankOne_scaled_projector_comparison_of_projected_eq_zero` closes the degenerate projected-residual subcase for the current scaled rank-one source-transpose handoff.  When `||(I-r r^+)p||_2^2 = 0`, the optimal scalar `c = (p^T r + t) / ||p||_2^2` makes the explicit right-projector comparison vanish on both sides, so this branch can feed the existing source-transpose certificate route.  This is still only a subcase: the nondegenerate case is already ruled out for the scalar-only route, and the full WKS source-block `sigma_min` upper branch still needs a stronger perturbation construction or a different source-specific comparison, plus the eigenvalue branch formula and `theta = infinity`.  No GPT Pro oracle consultation was used for this update.

Proof-source update: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorEtaF_le_formulaRHS_of_rankOne_scaled_source_transpose_projected_eq_zero` packages the degenerate projected-residual branch into the existing source-transpose upper handoff.  Given a nonzero source-block candidate `p`, nonzero source residual, nonzero optimal scale, branch selection `sigma_min <= phi`, zero projected component `||(I-r r^+)p||_2^2 = 0`, and the source-transpose certificate, it proves `eta_F(y) <=` the (20.21) right-hand side.  This removes one explicit right-projector obligation in the degenerate subcase; it does not supply the nonzero-scale condition automatically, solve the nondegenerate scalar obstruction, derive the full WKS source-block construction, prove the eigenvalue branch formula, or handle `theta = infinity`.  No GPT Pro oracle consultation was used for this update.

Proof-source update: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorRankOne_scaled_optimal_scale_num_eq_dot_b` and `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorRankOne_scaled_optimal_scale_eq_dot_b_div` expose the source-data form of the optimal scale used in the scaled rank-one WKS witness.  With `r = b - Ay` and `u = A^T p`, the numerator `p^T r + u^T y` is exactly `p^T b`, hence the optimal scale is `(p^T b)/||p||_2^2`.  This makes the nonzero-scale side condition in the degenerate source-transpose handoff auditable against the original right-hand side `b`; it does not prove that side condition, close the nondegenerate route, derive the full source-block construction, prove the eigenvalue branch formula, or handle `theta = infinity`.  No GPT Pro oracle consultation was used for this update.

Proof-source update: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorEtaF_le_formulaRHS_of_rankOne_scaled_source_transpose_projected_eq_zero_of_dot_b_ne_zero` strengthens the degenerate source-transpose handoff by replacing the optimal-scale nonzero hypothesis with the source-data condition `p^T b != 0`.  Together with the zero projected component, branch selection, and source-transpose certificate, it proves `eta_F(y) <=` the (20.21) right-hand side in that source-shaped degenerate subcase.  This still does not prove `p^T b != 0` for an arbitrary source-block singular vector, solve the nondegenerate obstruction, derive the full WKS source-block construction, prove the eigenvalue branch formula, or handle `theta = infinity`.  No GPT Pro oracle consultation was used for this update.

Proof-source update: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorEtaF_eq_formulaRHS_and_pos_of_rankOne_scaled_source_transpose_projected_eq_zero_of_dot_b_ne_zero` lifts the same source-shaped degenerate upper handoff to the finite-positive WKS equality/positivity surface.  Under `theta > 0`, `y != 0`, non-minimizer status, full row rank of `[A phi(I-r r^+)]`, zero projected component, `p^T b != 0`, branch selection, and the source-transpose certificate, it combines the degenerate `eta_F <= RHS` result with the already proved lower-bound side to prove `eta_F(y) = RHS` and positivity of both sides.  This is still a degenerate subcase only: it does not prove the source-dot condition for a row-side singular vector, solve the nondegenerate obstruction, derive the full WKS source-block construction, prove the eigenvalue branch formula, or handle `theta = infinity`.  No GPT Pro oracle consultation was used for this update.

- Latest source-route audit: the WKS red-bottleneck now has an explicit proof-source ledger entry.  The primary formula source is Waldén--Karlson--Sun (1995), DOI `10.1002/nla.1680020308`; direct paper-body inspection was blocked here, so no proof details from that paper are claimed.  The accessible route uses Chang--Golub--Paige--Titley-Peloquin, Sections 3-4, to start with the FLS/NeLS consistency characterization, then splits the remaining positive branch into the lower inequality `formulaRHS <= eta_F(y)` and the upper inequality `eta_F(y) <= formulaRHS`.  The next Lean work is a source-facing consistency-characterization theorem built on `RectLSNormalEquations.iff_isLeastSquaresMinimizer`, not another adjacent WKS wrapper.

These wrappers handle repeated singular values and the `alpha` left-null eigenspace from supplied component orthogonality, which the distinct-eigenvalue symmetric-matrix orthogonality lemma cannot cover.  This is still complete-basis infrastructure only: it does not prove singular-vector/nullspace basis existence, global multiplicities, or the matrix condition-number formula (20.19).

The positive branch and the magnitude of the negative branch are strictly ordered whenever the source singular values are strictly ordered.  This strengthens the extremal-branch/multiplicity route only: it does not prove the complete eigenbasis, global multiplicities, or the matrix condition-number formula (20.19).

The formal theorem keeps explicit denominator-positivity where division is used and records the nonnegative `eps`, `E`, and `f` majorant side conditions in the source predicate.

the exact transformed `[R;0]` QR solve formula is formalized by `LSAugmentedSystem.transformed_qr_solution`; the supplied-factor original-coordinate lift is formalized by `LSAugmentedSystem.exact_qr_solution_of_factors`; the exact asymmetric perturbed top-block handoff is formalized by `LSAsymmetricAugmentedSystem.exact_qr_solution_of_perturbed_triangular_solves`; the concrete triangular-solve handoff is formalized by `LSAsymmetricAugmentedSystem.exists_exact_qr_solution_of_fl_forwardSub_fl_backSub`; the exact lifted RHS perturbation handoff is formalized by `LSAsymmetricAugmentedSystem.exists_exact_qr_solution_of_fl_forwardSub_fl_backSub_transformed_rhs`; the concrete transformed-RHS/triangular handoff is formalized by `LSAsymmetricAugmentedSystem.exists_exact_qr_solution_of_fl_forwardSub_fl_backSub_of_fl_householderQRPanel_rhs`; the concrete QR/RHS/triangular handoff with Frobenius matrix perturbation is formalized by `LSAsymmetricAugmentedSystem.exists_exact_qr_solution_of_fl_householderQRPanel_solve_components`; the matrix-side `G|A|` Higham handoff is formalized by `LSAsymmetricAugmentedSystem.exists_exact_qr_solution_of_fl_householderQRPanel_higham_matrix_solve_components`; the zero-`Delta g` source package is formalized by `LSAsymmetricAugmentedSystem.exists_exact_qr_solution_of_fl_householderQRPanel_higham_matrix_solve_components_with_zero_deltag_bound`; the conditional uniform `Deltaf` source package with internally chosen `H1,H2` is formalized by `LSAsymmetricAugmentedSystem.exists_exact_qr_solution_of_fl_householderQRPanel_higham_matrix_solve_components_with_uniform_source_rhs_bound`; the implementation-backed growth-coefficient, closed-growth, gamma-only closed-growth, single-gamma-index, and factorized printed-radius `Deltaf` source packages without `hInfDom` are formalized by the `...with_growth_source_rhs_bound`, `...with_closed_growth_source_rhs_bound`, `...with_gamma_closed_growth_source_rhs_bound`, `...with_gamma_index_source_rhs_bound`, and `...with_gamma_factor_source_rhs_bound` wrappers; the scaled augmented matrix (20.17) is formalized by `lsScaledAugmentedMatrix` and its block-system iff; iterative-refinement algorithm spec, the remaining extra factor in the RHS coefficient, and final Theorem 20.4 packaging remain open. |
| Section 20.6 | CSNE method | corrected seminormal equations method and forward bound | DEFER | DEFER-MISSING-PRECISE-STATEMENT | Bound is rough/asymptotic; exact algorithm can be a benchmark. |

| `lsRealRectSigmaMinRow_pos_iff_forall_rowSingularValue_pos`, `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaMatrixSigmaMin_eq_zero_iff_exists_rowSingularValue_eq_zero` | positivity/zero bridge could be mistaken for a rank theorem or the source minimization formula | checked theorem surfaces against the row-side singular-value wrapper and the open Theorem 20.5 row | the theorems only relate the local `sigma_min` wrapper to the already-defined row-side singular values; they do not prove row-rank, do not connect the value to `eta_F(y)`, and do not prove the Walden-Karlson-Sun formula | `lake env lean LeanFpAnalysis/FP/Algorithms/LeastSquares/LSQRSolve.lean` passed | `LSQRSolve.lean` | passed |
| `normalEquationsCrossProductExampleRoundedGram_singular` | symbolic example with a modeled rounded cross-product matrix | checked against rendered source page 387 | theorem only proves singularity of the displayed rounded matrix, not that a concrete `FPModel` computes it | `lake env lean LeanFpAnalysis/FP/Algorithms/LeastSquares/LSNormalEquations.lean` passed | `LSNormalEquations.lean` | passed |

From a supplied exact transformed tall QR identity `Q^T B^T = [R;0]`, the bridge proves `B Q = [R^T 0]`, so the GQR constraint block has `S = R^T`; the triangularity theorem turns upper-triangular `R` into lower-triangular `S`.  This does not construct the QR factors, prove full GQR existence, or handle the transformed-`A` block reconstruction. It proves that local full-row-rank feasibility, null-intersection uniqueness, a supplied convergent exact weighted-minimizer branch, nonzero weights, and `(mu^2)^{-1} -> 0` give a unique exact LSE minimizer and convergence of that branch to it. Additional (20.26) increment: `lseWeightedMinimizer_tendsto_isLSEMinimizer_of_inv_mu_sq` was added as the combined inverse-square-weight branch-limit theorem for the method of weighting.  It proves that, if exact minimizers of the weighted unconstrained problems have a convergent branch, a feasible constrained comparator exists, all weights are nonzero, and `(mu^2)^{-1} -> 0`, then the branch limit is an exact LSE minimizer.  This removes the previous separate vector residual-convergence assumption by using the proved norm-residual convergence plus finite-dimensional coordinate convergence; it does not prove existence or continuity of a selected weighted minimizer branch, full convergence without a supplied branch, or finite-precision weighted-method stability. Additional (20.26) increment: `lseWeightedConstraintPenalty_le_objective`, `lseConstraintResidual_normSq_le_of_weightedObjective_le`, `lseConstraintResidual_norm_le_sqrt_div_of_weightedObjective_le`, and `lseWeightedMinimizer_constraintResidual_normSq_le_feasibleObjective_div_mu_sq` were added as finite-weight coercivity support for the method of weighting.  They prove that the weighted objective dominates `mu^2 * ||Bx-d||_2^2`, that any candidate with weighted objective at most `R` has constraint residual bounded by `R / mu^2` in squared norm, and that an exact minimizer of the weighted problem inherits such a bound from any feasible constrained comparator.  This does not prove convergence as `mu -> infinity`, existence/continuity of a selected minimizer branch, or any finite-precision weighted-method stability theorem. Additional (20.20)-(20.21) increment: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorEtaF_eq_zero_iff_isLeastSquaresMinimizer_of_positive_theta`, `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorEtaF_pos_iff_not_isLeastSquaresMinimizer_of_positive_theta`, `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaValue_pos_iff`, and `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaValue_eq_zero_iff` were added as zero/positivity bridges.  For positive finite `theta`, the first two prove that the normwise backward-error infimum `eta_F(y)` vanishes exactly when `y` is already an exact least-squares minimizer, and is positive exactly when it is not.  The latter two prove that the printed (20.21) right-hand side `min {phi, sigma_min [A phi(I-r r^+)]}` is positive exactly when both displayed branches are positive, and vanishes exactly when one branch vanishes.  This does not prove the Walden--Karlson--Sun spectral lower bound, construct an attaining feasible perturbation, prove equality with `eta_F`, derive the eigenvalue branch formula, or handle the `theta = infinity` limiting case. Additional (20.21) increment: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaMatrix_left_residual_col_sum_eq_zero`, `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaMatrix_right_residual_col_sum_eq_zero`, `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaMatrix_residual_leftNull_of_column_orthogonal`, and `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaMatrix_residual_leftNull_of_isLeastSquaresMinimizer` were added as the nonzero-residual left-null foundation for the WKS source block.  They prove that if a supplied residual is orthogonal to the data columns and nonzero, then it annihilates `[A phi(I-r r^+)]` from the left; in particular, an exact LS minimizer with nonzero Higham residual satisfies `r^T [A phi(I-r r^+)] = 0`.  This was a left-null-only foundation; the following increment adds row-rank deficiency and zero `sigma_min` for exact-minimizer branches, while the general lower-bound/attainment proof, eigenvalue formula, and `theta = infinity` remain open. Additional (20.21) increment: `lsRealRectRowRank_ne_card_of_leftNull`, `lsRealRectSigmaMinRow_eq_zero_of_leftNull`, `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaMatrixRowRank_ne_card_of_leftNull`, `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaMatrixSigmaMin_eq_zero_of_leftNull`, `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaMatrixSigmaMin_eq_zero_of_isLeastSquaresMinimizer`, `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaRHS_eq_zero_of_isLeastSquaresMinimizer_nonzero_residual`, and `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorEtaF_eq_formulaRHS_of_isLeastSquaresMinimizer` were added as the left-null-to-row-rank and exact-minimizer residual-branch closure for the WKS source block.  A nonzero vector annihilating every source-block column rules out full row rank and forces the row-side `sigma_min` branch to vanish; for an exact LS minimizer with nonzero residual this makes the printed RHS zero, and together with the existing zero-residual branch proves `eta_F(y)` equals the printed RHS for every exact LS minimizer.  This does not prove the general lower-bound/attainment theorem for non-minimizers, the eigenvalue branch formula, or `theta = infinity`. Additional (20.20)-(20.21) increment: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaRHS_eq_zero_of_isLeastSquaresMinimizer` and `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaRHS_eq_zero_of_etaF_eq_zero_of_positive_theta` were added as source-facing WKS zero-branch wrappers.  The first theorem packages both exact-minimizer residual branches into the printed right-hand side itself: if `y` is an exact least-squares minimizer, then `min {phi, sigma_min [A phi(I-r r^+)]} = 0`.  The second theorem combines the finite positive-`theta` zero-error characterization with that wrapper, proving that `eta_F(y) = 0` forces the printed RHS to vanish.  This does not prove a converse for all RHS-zero cases, the general Walden--Karlson--Sun lower-bound/attainment theorem for non-minimizers, the eigenvalue branch formula, or the `theta = infinity` limiting case. Additional (20.18) increment: `lsScaledAugmentedMatrix_singularPair_plus_minus_normalized_coefficients_eq_zero` and `lsScaledAugmentedMatrix_singularPair_plus_minus_leftNull_normalized_coefficients_eq_zero` were added as source-normalized coefficient-independence certificates for the printed scaled-augmented eigenvector shapes.  The two theorems transfer the existing unnormalized independence results for `[lambda_\pm u; sigma v]` to `[u; (sigma/lambda_\pm)v]`, and separate those printed singular-pair branches from a nonzero left-null branch `[w;0]`.  This is local multiplicity infrastructure only: it does not construct a complete singular-vector/nullspace basis, prove the global spectral decomposition, count source multiplicities, or connect the branches to the matrix condition number in (20.19). The shared generic theorem `lsScaledAugmentedMatrix_singularPair_normalized_eigenvector_of_quadratic` proves the printed vector shape `[u; (sigma/lambda) v]` whenever `lambda != 0` and satisfies the displayed quadratic; the plus and minus wrappers instantiate it with `lambda_+` and `lambda_-` under `alpha >= 0`, `sigma != 0`, and `v != 0`. Additional Theorem 20.9 associated-shape wrapper increment: `GQRAQTallAssocCase`, `GQRAQWideAssocCase`, `GQRAQTallAssocCase.mulVec_eq`, `GQRAQWideAssocCase.mulVec_eq`, `GeneralizedQRFactorization.exists_of_tall_qr_assoc_case`, and `GeneralizedQRFactorization.exists_of_wide_qr_assoc_case` were added to record and consume the associated-row/associated-column (20.28) shape hypotheses used by the construction route.  The wrappers reuse the existing supplied tall/wide QR packaging theorems, producing supplied (20.27) GQR data from exact `B^T` QR data and a supplied associated shape record.  This is exact supplied-shape algebra only: it does not construct `Q`, construct `U`, prove the shape records from actual factors, or prove computed GQR stability. Current exact-residual and zero-branch WKS branches: the source-residual hypothesis `lsResidualHigham A b y = 0` directly gives an exact least-squares minimizer, zero printed RHS, and `eta_F =` the printed (20.21) RHS.  For an exact minimizer with nonzero source residual, the residual annihilates the source block from the left, which now forces row-rank deficiency, `sigma_min = 0`, zero printed RHS, and `eta_F =` the printed RHS.  The wrapper `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaRHS_eq_zero_of_isLeastSquaresMinimizer` packages these branches, `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaRHS_eq_zero_of_etaF_eq_zero_of_positive_theta` adds the finite positive-`theta` zero-error-to-RHS-zero consistency direction, and `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorEtaF_eq_formulaRHS_of_etaF_eq_zero_of_positive_theta` packages the corresponding zero-error equality branch.  The zero-branch lower-bound wrappers now also prove `RHS <= eta_F` whenever the printed RHS is zero, in particular for exact minimizers and row-rank-deficient source blocks.  The converse-zero wrapper covers the nondegenerate case where the printed RHS is zero because `phi = 0`, forced by a positive row-side `sigma_min`; the non-minimizer classifiers prove that every remaining RHS-zero non-minimizer lies in the row-side `sigma_min = 0` branch, equivalently the row-rank-deficient branch; the global wrappers package these facts as zero iff `(exact minimizer or rowRank != m+1)` and positive iff `(not exact minimizer and rowRank = m+1)` for finite positive `theta` and nonzero `y`; the nondegenerate wrappers further show that under positive row-side `sigma_min`, and equivalently under full row rank of `[A phi(I-r r^+)]`, printed-RHS zero/positivity matches `eta_F` zero/positivity and a zero printed RHS gives the equality `eta_F = RHS`; the new left-panel theorem supplies that full source-block row rank whenever `A` itself has full row rank, and the full-left-panel wrappers use that theorem to make the printed-RHS zero/positivity and zero-equality consequences depend directly on full row rank of the original `A`; the eta/rank wrappers package zero iff `(eta_F=0 or rowRank != m+1)` and positive iff `(eta_F>0 and rowRank=m+1)`.  The remaining general WKS work is the positive nonzero-residual spectral lower-bound/attainment argument and the eigenvalue/limiting-case material.

Additional (20.20)-(20.21) zero-branch lower-bound increment: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaRHS_le_etaF_of_formulaRHS_eq_zero`, `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaRHS_le_etaF_of_isLeastSquaresMinimizer`, and `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaRHS_le_etaF_of_formulaMatrixRowRank_ne_card` were added.  The first theorem proves the lower-bound side `RHS <= eta_F(y)` for every zero printed-RHS branch by combining `RHS = 0` with nonnegativity of `eta_F`; the next two package exact-minimizer and row-rank-deficient source-block branches through that fact.  This closes the lower-bound handoff on zero branches only; it does not prove the positive-branch WKS spectral lower bound, construct an attaining perturbation, derive the eigenvalue branch formula, or handle the general `theta = infinity` limiting theorem. Additional (20.20)-(20.21) nondegenerate `eta_F`/RHS branch increment: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaRHS_eq_zero_iff_etaF_eq_zero_of_theta_pos_of_y_ne_zero_of_sigmaMin_pos` and `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaRHS_pos_iff_etaF_pos_of_theta_pos_of_y_ne_zero_of_sigmaMin_pos` were added.  They combine the finite positive-`theta` zero/positive `eta_F` characterizations with the global printed-RHS branch decomposition to prove that, for nonzero `y` and positive row-side `sigma_min [A phi(I-r r^+)]`, RHS zero is equivalent to `eta_F(y)=0`, and RHS positivity is equivalent to `0 < eta_F(y)`.  This is only the nondegenerate branch bridge; the degenerate `sigma_min = 0` branch, the Walden--Karlson--Sun lower-bound/attainment certificate, the eigenvalue branch formula, and the general `theta = infinity` limiting theorem remain open.  Validation: `lake env lean LeanFpAnalysis/FP/Algorithms/LeastSquares/LSQRSolve.lean`, `lake build LeanFpAnalysis.FP.Algorithms.LeastSquares.LSQRSolve`, focused `#print axioms` checks for the two new public theorems, touched-Lean-file placeholder/conflict/trailing-whitespace scans, `git diff --check`, and full `lake build` passed; axiom checks report only `propext`, `Classical.choice`, and `Quot.sound`, and the full build reported only pre-existing QR/Givens/FastMatMul warnings.

Additional (20.20)-(20.21) global branch-decomposition increment: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaRHS_eq_zero_iff_isLeastSquaresMinimizer_or_sigmaMin_eq_zero_of_theta_pos_of_y_ne_zero` and `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaRHS_pos_iff_not_isLeastSquaresMinimizer_and_sigmaMin_pos_of_theta_pos_of_y_ne_zero` were added.  They combine the exact-minimizer zero-RHS theorem with the non-minimizer branch classifiers to prove, for finite positive `theta` and nonzero `y`, that the printed RHS is zero iff `y` is an exact least-squares minimizer or the row-side `sigma_min` branch is zero, and positive iff `y` is not a minimizer and the row-side `sigma_min` branch is positive.  This is a branch-decomposition wrapper only; it does not prove the Walden--Karlson--Sun lower-bound/attainment certificate, the eigenvalue branch formula, or the general `theta = infinity` limiting theorem. Additional (20.20)-(20.21) non-minimizer branch-classification increment: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorPhi_pos_of_not_isLeastSquaresMinimizer_of_theta_pos_of_y_ne_zero`, `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaRHS_eq_zero_iff_sigmaMin_eq_zero_of_not_isLeastSquaresMinimizer`, and `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaRHS_pos_iff_sigmaMin_pos_of_not_isLeastSquaresMinimizer` were added.  They prove that, for finite positive `theta`, nonzero `y`, and a non-minimizer candidate, the printed scalar branch `phi` is strictly positive; hence RHS zero is equivalent to the degenerate row-side `sigma_min = 0` branch, and RHS positivity is equivalent to positive row-side `sigma_min`.  This narrows the remaining WKS formula work to the spectral lower/attainment certificate on the nonzero positive-branch case and the eigenvalue/limiting-case material. Additional (20.20)-(20.21) nondegenerate converse-zero increment: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorMu_pos_of_theta_pos_of_y_ne_zero`, `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorPhi_eq_zero_iff_residual_eq_zero_of_theta_pos_of_y_ne_zero`, and `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorEtaF_eq_formulaRHS_of_formulaRHS_eq_zero_of_sigmaMin_pos` were added.  They prove that, for finite positive `theta` and nonzero `y`, the scalar `phi` is zero exactly when the source residual is zero; therefore a zero printed RHS with positive row-side `sigma_min [A phi(I-r r^+)]` collapses to the exact-residual branch and gives `eta_F(y) = RHS`.  This does not prove the degenerate `sigma_min = 0` converse branch, the general WKS lower-bound/attainment certificate, the eigenvalue branch formula, or the general `theta = infinity` limiting theorem. Additional (20.20)-(20.21) increment: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaRHS_pos_iff` and `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaRHS_eq_zero_iff` were added as source-data branch-characterization wrappers for the printed RHS.  They substitute Higham's residual convention into the existing supplied-residual `min {phi, sigma_min}` positivity/zero theorems, proving exactly which displayed branch conditions make the source-data RHS positive or zero.  This supports the remaining WKS route by isolating the nonzero branch case, but it does not prove `RHS = 0 -> eta_F(y) = 0`, the general lower-bound/attainment certificate, the eigenvalue branch formula, or the `theta = infinity` limiting case.


Additional (20.18) spectral orthogonality increment: `isSymmetricFiniteMatrix_eigenvectors_sum_mul_eq_zero`, `lsScaledAugmentedMatrix_eigenvectors_sum_mul_eq_zero`, `lsScaledAugmentedMatrix_singularPair_plus_minus_normalized_dot_eq_zero`, `lsScaledAugmentedMatrix_singularPair_plus_leftNull_normalized_dot_eq_zero`, and `lsScaledAugmentedMatrix_singularPair_minus_leftNull_normalized_dot_eq_zero` were added. Additional (20.24) LSE uniqueness bridge increment: `exists_unique_isLSEMinimizer_iff_nullIntersectionTrivial_of_exists` was added.  It proves that, once an exact equality-constrained least-squares minimizer exists, existence-and-uniqueness of that minimizer is equivalent to the null-intersection condition in (20.24).  The forward direction shifts a minimizer by a common null vector and uses objective invariance; the reverse direction reuses `IsLSEMinimizer.eq_of_nullIntersectionTrivial`.  This is exact LSE algebra only: it does not prove full-row-rank minimizer existence, GQR factor construction, associated (20.28) shape construction, or computed GQR stability.  Validation started with baseline and post-edit `lake env lean LeanFpAnalysis/FP/Algorithms/LeastSquares/LSE.lean`; full milestone validation is recorded for this commit.

Additional (20.24) stacked full-column-rank uniqueness bridge increment: `exists_unique_isLSEMinimizer_iff_lseStackedFullColumnRank_of_exists` was added.  It restates the existing-minimizer uniqueness iff in the source wording that `[A^T,B^T]^T` has full column rank, represented locally by injectivity of the vertical stack `[A;B]`.  This is an exact corollary of `exists_unique_isLSEMinimizer_iff_nullIntersectionTrivial_of_exists` and `LSENullIntersectionTrivial.iff_lseStackedFullColumnRank`; it does not prove numeric rank equivalence, full-row-rank minimizer existence, GQR construction, associated (20.28) shape construction, or computed GQR stability.  Validation started with baseline and post-edit `lake env lean LeanFpAnalysis/FP/Algorithms/LeastSquares/LSE.lean`; full milestone validation is recorded for this commit.

The first theorem gives direct uniqueness of any two exact LSE minimizers from the local stacked full-column-rank condition; the second composes that source-rank wording with the supplied-GQR exact minimizer theorem, using full-row-rank consistency and stacked full-column rank at the public surface.  This is exact supplied-factor algebra only: it does not prove numeric rank equivalence, construct the GQR factors, derive associated (20.28) shapes from actual QR factors, or prove computed GQR stability. Additional Theorem 20.9 orthogonal-completion increment: `exists_orthogonal_completion_tall_qr_block` was added. Additional Theorem 20.9 MGS orthogonality atom increment: `gsDot_self_eq_finiteVecNorm2Sq`, `gsDot_projectAway_self`, `gsDot_projectAway_eq_zero_of_unit`, and `modifiedGramSchmidtQ_dot_vectors_succ_later_eq_zero` were added in the QR Gram-Schmidt layer.  The source-facing step theorem proves that after exact MGS step `k`, each later residual column is orthogonal to the current normalized `q_k` column. Additional Theorem 20.9 MGS orthogonality-persistence increment: `gsDot_projectAway_left` and `gsDot_projectAway_eq_zero_of_left_orthogonal` were added. This is the second local algebra atom for the full MGS orthonormality induction; it still does not assemble the induction over stages/column pairs. Additional Theorem 20.9 MGS conditional orthogonality bridge increment: `gsDot_normalize_right`, `modifiedGramSchmidtQ_dot_vectors_stage_eq_zero_of_lt_of_prev`, and `modifiedGramSchmidtQ_dot_eq_zero_of_lt_of_prev` were added.  The new stage theorem carries an older `q_i` residual orthogonality relation from stage `i+1` through stage `j` assuming the intervening normalized columns are already orthogonal to `q_i`, and the pair theorem transfers that residual result to the final normalized `q_j`.  This is the induction bridge for the full MGS orthonormal-columns route; it still leaves the final unconditional strong induction over column pairs and the downstream `U`/associated-shape GQR construction open. Additional Theorem 20.9 MGS pairwise orthogonality increment: `modifiedGramSchmidtQ_dot_eq_zero_of_lt` was added.  Under the standard nonzero-stage MGS hypothesis, it proves every earlier normalized column `q_i` is orthogonal to every later normalized column `q_j` by strong induction over the later column and the conditional stage bridge above.  This closes the off-diagonal MGS orthogonality dependency; the next remaining MGS package step is turning unit column norms plus pairwise dot-zero into `GramSchmidtOrthonormalColumns (modifiedGramSchmidtQ A)`. The package theorem combines the already proved unit column norm result and pairwise dot-zero theorem to prove `GramSchmidtOrthonormalColumns (modifiedGramSchmidtQ A)` from the standard nonzero-stage MGS hypothesis.  This closes the QR-side orthonormality dependency for the exact `B^T` MGS factorization route; the next Theorem 20.9 work is to use it to remove the orthonormality assumption from the GQR constraint-block construction and then build the `U`/associated-shape side.  Validation: `lake env lean LeanFpAnalysis/FP/Algorithms/QR/GramSchmidt.lean` and `git diff --check -- LeanFpAnalysis/FP/Algorithms/QR/GramSchmidt.lean` passed after merging latest `origin/main`; no oracle consultation was used for this update.

Additional Theorem 20.9 MGS-to-GQR constraint-block increment: `exists_transpose_tall_qr_of_mgs` and `exists_gqr_constraint_block_of_mgs` were added.  These wrappers use `modifiedGramSchmidtQ_orthonormal_columns` to remove the explicit orthonormality hypothesis from the previous exact MGS `B^T` QR and GQR constraint-block construction, so only the nonzero MGS stage-normalizer hypothesis remains on the QR side.  This closes the `B Q = [S 0]` construction route under exact MGS data; it still does not construct the `U` factor for `A Q`, prove the associated tall/wide shape records, or package the full Theorem 20.9 reconstruction. These theorems consume exact MGS nonzero-stage data for `B^T`, construct the GQR constraint side internally, and package a full `GeneralizedQRFactorization` whenever the remaining `A Q` side supplies an associated tall or wide `U^T A Q` shape for the completed `Q`. This removes the completely opaque wide associated-shape assumption for that supplied trailing-block QR route, but it still does not instantiate that route for the actual `A Q` selected by the MGS `B^T` construction, does not construct the tall associated shape, and does not close the full Theorem 20.9 reconstruction. Additional Theorem 20.9 rank-to-MGS nonbreakdown base increment: `rectMatMulVec_finiteBasisVec_gsColumn` and `modifiedGramSchmidtVectors_zero_norm_ne_zero_of_rectMatMulVec_injective` were added in the Gram-Schmidt layer.  The new dependency proves the base case of the rank-to-MGS route: an injective rectangular column map rules out a zero input column and therefore rules out a zero stage-0 MGS normalizer.  This starts discharging the explicit MGS nonzero-stage hypotheses used by the exact GQR construction, but it does not yet prove the full induction over later MGS residual stages or specialize full row rank of `B` to injectivity of `B^T`. Additional Theorem 20.9 all-stage rank-to-MGS nonbreakdown increment: `modifiedGramSchmidtVectors_exists_source_coeffs` and `modifiedGramSchmidtVectors_norm_ne_zero_of_rectMatMulVec_injective` were added in the QR Gram-Schmidt layer.  The first theorem proves that every exact MGS residual is a linear combination of the original columns with coefficient `1` on its own source column and zero coefficients on later source columns; the second uses that invariant to show an injective rectangular column map rules out zero active residuals at every MGS stage.  This closes the later-stage nonbreakdown induction that was still open after the stage-0 bridge, but it does not by itself construct the tall associated shape, prove numeric rank equivalence, or prove computed GQR stability. GPT Pro oracle consultation log, Theorem 20.9 GQR A-side route: consulted after local work showed that deriving MGS nonbreakdown for the full wide trailing `gqrAQWideAssocL (A Q)` block from the source rank assumptions is likely too strong.  Prompt summary: asked for a source-faithful construction of the `U^T A Q` associated shape without assuming nonbreakdown for a possibly rank-deficient block, comparing rank-tolerant triangularization, smaller full-rank subblock QR, and block/kernel arguments.  Answer summary: recommended proving the kernel consequence `A` injective on `ker B`, identifying `range Q2 = ker B` after `B Q = [S 0]` with `S` nonsingular, deriving injectivity of `A Q2`, and applying QR/MGS only to that safe `Q2` block before extending to a full orthogonal `U`; it explicitly warned against QR/MGS on the full wide trailing block.  Adopted status: partially adopted in Lean via `GeneralizedQRFactorization.A_Q2_kernel_trivial_of_*`, `GeneralizedQRFactorization.A_Q2_rectMatMulVec_injective_of_*`, and `GeneralizedQRFactorization.A_Q2_mgs_norm_ne_zero_of_*`; the next local target is to use this smaller-block MGS bridge to build the associated (20.28) shape without assuming nonbreakdown for the whole trailing block.  Verification result: focused `lake env lean LeanFpAnalysis/FP/Algorithms/LeastSquares/LSE.lean` checks passed for both Lean milestones, and each milestone was committed, merged with latest `origin/main`, and pushed to both the working branch and `main`.

Additional Theorem 20.9 Q2-kernel increment: `GeneralizedQRFactorization.A_Q2_kernel_trivial_of_nullIntersectionTrivial` proves the oracle-recommended kernel bridge at the supplied-GQR surface: if `A (Q [0; y2]) = 0`, then `Q [0; y2]` also satisfies the `B` constraint block equation, so the local null-intersection condition forces `y2 = 0`.  `GeneralizedQRFactorization.A_Q2_kernel_trivial_of_stackedFullColumnRank` exposes the same result under the source stacked-full-column-rank hypothesis by reusing `LSENullIntersectionTrivial.iff_lseStackedFullColumnRank`.  This is still supplied-GQR block algebra: it does not construct `Q`, construct `U`, prove the associated (20.28) shape, or prove computed GQR stability.  Validation: `lake env lean LeanFpAnalysis/FP/Algorithms/LeastSquares/LSE.lean`, `git diff --check -- LeanFpAnalysis/FP/Algorithms/LeastSquares/LSE.lean`, merge with latest `origin/main`, and push to branch and `main` passed.

Additional Theorem 20.9 AQ2 MGS increment: `gqrAQ2Block` and `gqrAQ2Block_mulVec` name the smaller trailing source block `A Q2` and its vector action.  `GeneralizedQRFactorization.A_Q2_rectMatMulVec_injective_of_nullIntersectionTrivial` and `GeneralizedQRFactorization.A_Q2_rectMatMulVec_injective_of_stackedFullColumnRank` convert the Q2 kernel bridge into injectivity of that rectangular column map, and `GeneralizedQRFactorization.A_Q2_mgs_norm_ne_zero_of_nullIntersectionTrivial` plus `GeneralizedQRFactorization.A_Q2_mgs_norm_ne_zero_of_stackedFullColumnRank` feed that injectivity into the exact-MGS all-stage nonbreakdown theorem.  This closes the oracle-recommended nonbreakdown input for the smaller `A Q2` block, but still does not build the full associated (20.28) shape, construct the final `U`, or prove computed GQR stability.
